<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">NASHUA, N.H. &#8211;&nbsp; November 13, 2024&nbsp; &#8211; iCAD, Inc. <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10pt;font-variant:normal;margin:0pt 0pt 0pt 8pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt 7pt;">"We made continued progress during the third quarter highlighted by growing market interest which resulted in the close of 52 perpetual deals, 20 subscription deals, and 13 cloud deals in the quarter. Our ProFound Cloud SaaS platform, launched at the end of the first quarter of 2024, is achieving adoption rates ahead of our expectations, and as a result, annual recurring revenue increased by 10% in the third quarter,&#8221; commented Dana Brown, President and CEO of iCAD. &#8220;Earlier this week, we also announced FDA clearance of ProFound Detection Version 4.0 for Digital Breast Tomosynthesis (DBT). This fourth-generation AI solution, powered by advanced deep learning convolutional neural networks, offers a 22% improvement in detecting challenging and aggressive cancer subtypes over prior Version 3, including enhanced accuracy for dense breast tissue. Additionally, ProFound Detection Version 4.0 achieves an 18% reduction in lesion markings, minimizing false positives and streamlining workflow. This milestone reinforces iCAD&#8217;s commitment to advancing breast health by delivering solutions that elevate clinical confidence, enhance the experience and confidence of our clinicians, and improve patient outcomes.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt 7pt;">"Likewise, we expanded our presence across key markets to extend our geographic reach, reflecting new regulatory clearances in South Africa and partnerships in the Dominican Republic, France, Spain, Turkey, and the United Arab Emirates. Additionally, during the quarter, the FDA&#8217;s new regulations around breast density reporting in the U.S. came into effect, and we believe this development will bolster demand for our Density and Detection solutions. We remain focused on continuing to position iCAD to strengthen our market leadership in AI-powered breast cancer detection and drive the global scalability of our solutions."</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Gross Profit: Gross profit for the&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="5x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776667996">September 30, 2024</a> was $12.0&nbsp;million, or 84% of revenue, as compared to $10.5&nbsp;million, or 83% of revenue, in the <a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended <a data-tblloc="6x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776684064">September 30, 2023</a>.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Operating Expenses: Total operating expenses for the&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="5x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776667996">September 30, 2024</a> were $17.4&nbsp;million, consistent with&nbsp;the <a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended <a data-tblloc="6x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776684064">September 30, 2023</a>.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">GAAP Net&nbsp;Loss from continuing operations: Net loss from continuing operations for the&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="5x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776667996">September 30, 2024</a> was ($4.8) million, or ($0.18)&nbsp;per diluted share, as compared to a net loss of ($6.5) million, or ($0.25) per diluted share, for the <a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended <a data-tblloc="6x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776684064">September 30, 2023</a>.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Non-GAAP Adjusted Net Loss from continuing operations: Non-GAAP Adjusted Net Loss from continuing operations, a non-GAAP financial measure as defined below, for the&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="5x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776667996">September 30, 2024</a> was ($4.6) million, or ($0.18) per diluted share, as compared to a Non-GAAP Adjusted Net Loss of ($6.3)&nbsp;million, or ($0.25) per diluted share, for the <a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended <a data-tblloc="6x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776684064">September 30, 2023</a>. Please refer to the section entitled &#8220;Reconciliation of Non-GAAP Financial Measures to Comparable GAAP Measures&#8221; and the accompanying financial table included at the end of this release for a reconciliation of GAAP Net Loss to Non-GAAP Adjusted Net Loss results for the <a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a>-month periods ended <a data-tblloc="7x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F20233211682094343599">September 30, 2024 and 2023</a>, respectively.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Non-GAAP Adjusted EBITDA: Non-GAAP Adjusted EBITDA, a non-GAAP financial measure as defined below, for the&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended&nbsp;<a data-tblloc="5x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776667996">September 30, 2024</a> was a loss of ($3.9) million compared to a loss of $(5.4)&nbsp;million in the <a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a> months ended <a data-tblloc="6x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F2024571717776684064">September 30, 2023</a>.&nbsp;Please refer to the section entitled &#8220;Reconciliation of Non-GAAP Financial Measures to Comparable GAAP Measures&#8221; and the accompanying financial table included at the end of this release for a reconciliation of GAAP Net Loss to Non-GAAP Adjusted EBITDA results for the <a data-tblloc="49x1" data-tblname="395578" data-tblv="3" id="led395578F2024571717776650455">nine</a>-month periods ended <a data-tblloc="7x1" data-tblname="395579" data-tblv="3" id="led395579F20233211682094348933">September 30, 2024 and 2023</a>, respectively.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Cash and cash equivalents:&#8239; Cash&nbsp;and cash equivalents were $18.8&nbsp;million as of September 30,&nbsp;2024. &nbsp;iCAD&nbsp;believes it has sufficient cash resources to fund its planned operations with no need to raise additional funding.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt -1pt;"><b>Use of Non-GAAP Financial Measures </b></p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt -1pt;">In its quarterly news releases, conference calls, slide presentations or webcasts, the Company may use or discuss non-GAAP financial measures as defined by SEC Regulation G. The GAAP financial measures most directly comparable to each non-GAAP financial measure used or discussed, and a reconciliation of the differences between each non-GAAP financial measure and the comparable GAAP financial measure, are included in this press release after the condensed consolidated financial statements. When analyzing the Company&#8217;s operating performance, investors should not consider these non-GAAP measures as a substitute for the comparable financial measures prepared in accordance with GAAP. The Company&#8217;s quarterly news releases containing such non-GAAP reconciliations can be found on the Investors section of the Company&#8217;s website at www.icadmed.com</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt -1pt;"><b>About iCAD, Inc.</b></p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt -1pt;">iCAD, Inc. (NASDAQ: ICAD) is a global leader on a mission to create a world where cancer can&#8217;t hide by providing clinically proven AI-powered solutions that enable medical providers to accurately and reliably detect cancer earlier and improve patient outcomes. Headquartered in Nashua, N.H., iCAD&#8217;s industry-leading ProFound Breast Health Suite provides AI-powered mammography analysis for breast cancer detection, density assessment and risk evaluation. Used by thousands of providers serving millions of patients, ProFound is available in over 50 countries. In the last five years alone, iCAD estimates reading more than 40 million mammograms worldwide, with nearly 30% being tomosynthesis.&nbsp; For more information, including the latest in regulatory clearances, please visit www.icadmed.com.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt 8pt;">&nbsp;</p>

Such forward-looking statements involve a number of known and unknown risks, uncertainties, and other factors that may cause the actual results, performance, or achievements of the Company to be materially different from any future results, performance, or achievements expressed or implied by such forward-looking statements. Such factors include, but are not limited, to the Company&#8217;s ability to achieve business and strategic objectives, the willingness of patients to undergo mammography screening, whether mammography screening will be treated as an essential procedure, whether ProFound AI will improve reading efficiency, improve specificity and sensitivity, reduce false positives and otherwise prove to be more beneficial for patients and clinicians, the impact of supply and manufacturing constraints or difficulties on our ability to fulfill our orders, uncertainty of future sales levels, to defend itself in litigation matters, protection of patents and other proprietary rights, product market acceptance, possible technological obsolescence of products, increased competition, government regulation, changes in Medicare or<b> </b>other reimbursement policies, risks relating to our existing and future debt obligations, competitive factors, the effects of a decline in the economy or markets served by the Company; and other risks detailed in the Company&#8217;s filings with the Securities and Exchange Commission. <p style="font-size: 11pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;"><b>Reconciliation of Non-GAAP Financial Measures to Comparable GAAP Measures and Definitions of Metrics</b></p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">The Company reports its financial results in accordance with United States generally accepted accounting principles, or GAAP. However, management believes that in order to understand the Company&#8217;s short-term and long-term financial and operational trends, investors may wish to consider the impact of certain non-cash or non-recurring items, when used as a supplement to financial performance measures in accordance with GAAP. These items result from facts and circumstances that vary in frequency and/or impact on continuing operations. Management also uses results of operations before such items to evaluate the operating performance of the Company and compare it against past periods, make operating decisions, and serve as a basis for strategic planning. These non-GAAP financial measures provide management with additional means to understand and evaluate the operating results and trends in the Company&#8217;s ongoing business by eliminating certain non-cash expenses and other items that management believes might otherwise make comparisons of the Company&#8217;s ongoing business with prior periods more difficult, obscure trends in ongoing operations or reduce management&#8217;s ability to make useful forecasts. Management believes that these non-GAAP financial measures provide additional means of evaluating period-over-period operating performance. In addition, management understands that some investors and financial analysts find this information helpful in analyzing the Company&#8217;s financial and operational performance and comparing this performance to its peers and competitors.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Management defines &#8220;Non-GAAP Adjusted EBITDA&#8221; as the sum of GAAP Net Loss before provisions for interest expense, other income, stock-based compensation expense, depreciation and amortization, tax expense, severance, gain on sale of assets, loss on disposal of assets, acquisition and litigation related expenses. Management considers this non-GAAP financial measure to be an indicator of the Company&#8217;s operational strength and performance of its business and a good measure of its historical operating trends, in particular the extent to which ongoing operations impact the Company&#8217;s overall financial performance.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">The non-GAAP financial measures do not replace the presentation of the Company&#8217;s GAAP financial results and should only be used as a supplement to, not as a substitute for, the Company&#8217;s financial results presented in accordance with GAAP. The Company has provided a reconciliation of each non-GAAP financial measure used in its financial reporting and investor presentations to the most directly comparable GAAP financial measure.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Management excludes each of the items identified below from the applicable non-GAAP financial measure referenced above for the reasons set forth with respect to that excluded item:</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; text-indent: 0px; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 27pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&#8226;</p>
			</td>
			<td style="width: auto; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Interest expense: The Company excludes interest expense which includes interest from the facility agreement, interest on capital leases and interest on the convertible debentures from its non-GAAP Adjusted EBITDA calculation.</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; text-indent: 0px; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 27pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&#8226;</p>
			</td>
			<td style="width: auto; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Stock-based compensation expense: excluded as these are non-cash expenses that management does not consider part of ongoing operating results when assessing the performance of the Company&#8217;s business, and also because the total amount of expense is partially outside of the Company&#8217;s control as it is based on factors such as stock price volatility and interest rates, which may be unrelated to our performance during the period in which the expense is incurred.</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; text-indent: 0px; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 27pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&#8226;</p>
			</td>
			<td style="width: auto; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Amortization and Depreciation: Purchased assets and intangibles are amortized over a period of several years and generally cannot be changed or influenced by management after they are acquired. Accordingly, these non-cash items are not considered by management in making operating decisions, and management believes that such expenses do not have a direct correlation to future business operations. Thus, including such charges does not accurately reflect the performance of the Company&#8217;s ongoing operations for the period in which such charges are incurred.</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; text-indent: 0px; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 27pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&#8226;</p>
			</td>
			<td style="width: auto; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Severance and Furlough: The Company has incurred severance and furlough expenses in connection with restructuring and in connection with the separation of its former CEO.&nbsp; The Company excludes these items from its non-GAAP financial measures when evaluating its continuing business performance as such&nbsp;items can vary significantly and do not reflect expected future operating expenses. In addition, management believes that such items do not have a direct correlation to future business operations.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

The Company excludes this non-cash item as it is not considered by management in making operating decisions, and management believes that such item does not have a direct correlation to future business operations.</p>

The Company excludes these costs from its non-GAAP measures primarily because the Company believes that these costs have no direct correlation to the core operations of the Company.</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt -1pt;"><b><u>Definitions of Metrics</u></b></p>

<p style="font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt 0pt 0pt -1pt;">Starting in the third quarter of 2023, the Company began reporting Annual Recurring Revenue (&#8220;ARR&#8221;) with each quarterly earnings announcement.&nbsp; The Company&#8217;s management believes this is a useful metric for purposes of assessing progress in transitioning to a subscription-based business model.&nbsp; ARR should be viewed independently of revenue and does not represent our revenue under U.S. GAAP on an annualized basis, as it is an operating metric that can be impacted by contract start dates, end dates, cancellations, and renewal rates. Subscription ARR is not intended to be a replacement for forecasts of revenue. &nbsp;The following are the variations of ARR the Company intends to present:</p>

<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">&nbsp;</p>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 37pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">1.</p>
			</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Total ARR (T-ARR) represents the annualized value of subscription license, maintenance contracts and active cloud services at the end of a reporting period.</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 37pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">2.</p>
			</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Maintenance Services ARR (M-ARR) represents the annualized value of active perpetual license maintenance service contracts at the end of the reporting period.&nbsp;</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 37pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">3.</p>
			</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Subscription ARR (S-ARR) represents the annualized value of active subscription or term licenses at the end of a reporting period.</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>

<table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width: 100%; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">

		<tr style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<td style="width: 37pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">&nbsp;</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; width: 18pt; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">4.</p>
			</td>
			<td style="vertical-align: top; font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt;">
			<p style="font-family: Calibri, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; font-variant: normal; margin: 0pt;">Cloud ARR (C-ARR) represents the annualized value of active cloud services contracts at the end of a reporting period.</p>
			</td>
		</tr>

</table>
